data-ref-id="3030-11151">X-Squad</a></li></ul><h2>Online</h2><p>Before the launch of Microsoft's online capable <a href="/xbox/3045-32/" data-ref-id="3045-32">Xbox</a>, Sony placed little emphasis on online gaming during the PlayStation 2's early years. In 2002, however, Sony began heavily advertising several online first-party titles, such as <a href="/socom-us-navy-seals/3030-6246/" data-ref-id="3030-6246">SOCOM: US Navy Seals</a>. Although late, and despite the fact that Sony required developers to pick up the responsibility of providing servers, online gaming was one of the major selling points of the PlayStation 2. The original PlayStation 2 consoles did not have an integrated network adapter, requiring instead that the user purchase the unit separately. The launch of the PlayStation 2 Slim model saw the network adapter built into the console.</p><h2>PlayStation 2 Slim</h2><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/3/30036/909758-image.php.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-909758" data-size="small" data-ratio="1" data-width="400" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 400px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:100.0%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/3/30036/909758-image.php.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-909758"><img alt="PS2 Slim" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/3/30036/909758-image.php.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/3/30036/909758-image.php.jpg 400w" sizes="(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px" data-width="640"></a><figcaption>PS2 Slim</figcaption></figure><p>In September 2004, in time for the launch of <a href="/grand-theft-auto-san-andreas/3030-7120/" data-ref-id="3030-7120">Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas</a>, Sony unveiled one of its major hardware revisions: a smaller, thinner and quieter PlayStation 2 that included a built-in Ethernet port. Called the PS2 Slim, it did not contain a 3.5" expansion bay, thus removing support for an internal hard disk drive. Similar to the <a href="/gamecube/3045-23/" data-ref-id="3045-23">GameCube</a>, early models lacked an internal power supply, and had a modified multi-tap expansion. Later models of the PlayStation 2 Slim do not require an external power supply. The removal of the expansion bay was criticized as a limitation due to the existence of titles such as <a href="/final-fantasy-xi-online/3030-11142/" data-ref-id="3030-11142">Final Fantasy XI</a>, which required the use of the HDD. The PlayStation 2 Slim model was first released in black, however today the slimline model can be found in silver, white, and pink in North America.</p><h2>PSX</h2><p>The Sony PSX (not to be confused with the PlayStation) is a consumer device that can be used as a digital video recorder, DVD burner, and PS2 game player. It also includes built in video, photo, and audio editing software. The device, which has only released in Japan, was poorly received, with some major features absent from the first editions of the hardware. Despite major price drops on the device, sales were very weak in Japan. It is still notable for introduction of the popular XMB interface, now used in Sony's PSP, PlayStation 3, and Bravia TVs.</p><h2>Accessories and Peripherals</h2><table><tbody><tr><td><h3>DualShock 2</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-970716" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.67068273092369" data-width="498" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 498px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:67.1%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-970716"><img alt="DualShock 2" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg 498w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="DualShock 2" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg 498w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/1/14741/970716-dualshock2.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a><figcaption>DualShock 2</figcaption></figure> The <a href="../../dualshock-2/59-30/" rel="nofollow">DualShock 2</a> is the standard controller which comes packaged with the PS2. Visually, it was practically identical to the original <a href="/dualshock-controller/3000-1/" data-ref-id="3000-1">DualShock</a>, with the main distinction being its black color. The controller included rumble and had the same button layout as its predecessor, but was lighter, had more accurate analog movement, and featured pressure sensitive buttons. The DualShock 2 is regarded as one of the best controllers ever made, despite some criticisms of parallel analog sticks, shallow buttons, and questionable ergonomics.</td></tr><tr><td><h3>EyeToy</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/3766/560739-eyetoy.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-560739" data-size="small" data-ratio="1.0531561461794" data-width="301" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 301px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:105.3%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/3766/560739-eyetoy.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-560739"><img alt="EyeToy Camera" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 301px) 100vw, 301px" data-width="301" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/3766/560739-eyetoy.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/3766/560739-eyetoy.jpg 301w"><noscript><img alt="EyeToy Camera" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/3766/560739-eyetoy.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/3766/560739-eyetoy.jpg 301w" sizes="(max-width: 301px) 100vw, 301px" data-width="301"></noscript></a><figcaption>EyeToy Camera</figcaption></figure> One of the most well known of all the PS2's peripherals is the <a href="/eyetoy/3025-178/" data-ref-id="3025-178">EyeToy</a>. It was a USB vision camera which took images of what the player was doing and relayed it back into games so the player could interact with games using motion. The camera was mainly used with the nine games of the <a href="../../eyetoy/62-178/" rel="nofollow">EyeToy</a> franchise but also with other games that used the device's capabilities, such as <a href="/dance-dance-revolution-extreme/3030-3280/" data-ref-id="3030-3280">Dance Dance Revolution EXTREME</a>, although the EyeToy isn't integral to the gameplay experience in most of these games. The camera has serious limitation; it has roughly 1.3 megapixels, and needed a lot of light in the playing area. A red LED turns on when EyeToy doesn't have enough light to distinguish the player from the background.</td></tr><tr><td><h3>PS2 HDD</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1125682" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.75" data-width="800" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 800px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:75.0%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1125682"><img alt="PS2 HDD" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg 800w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="PS2 HDD" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg 800w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/1/14741/1125682-800px_playstation_bb_unit.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a><figcaption>PS2 HDD</figcaption></figure> Released in North America and Japan, the PlayStation 2 Hard Drive Disk allowed for the storage of up to 40GB. The HDD could be used to reduce load times by caching data on the hard drive. Few North American games had HDD support, and the only game which actually needed the drive was <a href="../../final-fantasy-xi-online/61-11142/" rel="nofollow">Final Fantasy XI</a>, as it was used to store patches and other game updates. In 2004, the device stopped receiving support from Sony. The Slimline model can't use the HDD without a 3rd party cable.</td></tr></tbody></table><h2>Best Selling Games</h2><ul><li><a href="/grand-theft-auto-san-andreas/3030-7120/" data-ref-id="3030-7120">Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas</a> - <h2>Overview</h2><p>The Xbox 360, the second video game console from <a href="/microsoft-game-studios/3010-340/" data-ref-id="3010-340">Microsoft Corporation</a>, was officially unveiled on May 12, 2005 during a special presentation show that aired live on MTV.</p><p>Co-Developed with <a href="/ibm/3010-190/" data-ref-id="3010-190">IBM</a>, <a href="/ati-technologies-inc/3010-5494/" data-ref-id="3010-5494">ATI</a>, and Silicon Integrated Systems, the Xbox 360 uses the triple-core IBM designed Xenon as its CPU, ATI Xenos which has 10 MB of embedded eDRAM as the graphics processor and has a main memory pool of 512 MB. Development of the Xbox 360 began in early 2003, a year and a half after the original <a href="/xbox/3045-32/" data-ref-id="3045-32">Xbox</a> release.</p><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/8272/1865878-4489046b_6599_4ab9_ae7d_9ade49fa0252_copy.png" data-ref-id="1300-1865878" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.20313790255987" data-width="1211" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 1211px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:20.3%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/8272/1865878-4489046b_6599_4ab9_ae7d_9ade49fa0252_copy.png" data-ref-id="1300-1865878"><img alt="New Xbox 360 logo" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/8272/1865878-4489046b_6599_4ab9_ae7d_9ade49fa0252_copy.png" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/8272/1865878-4489046b_6599_4ab9_ae7d_9ade49fa0252_copy.png 1211w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_super/0/8272/1865878-4489046b_6599_4ab9_ae7d_9ade49fa0252_copy.png 960w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/0/8272/1865878-4489046b_6599_4ab9_ae7d_9ade49fa0252_copy.png 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/8272/1865878-4489046b_6599_4ab9_ae7d_9ade49fa0252_copy.png 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></a><figcaption>New Xbox 360 logo</figcaption></figure><p>Following the official unveil on MTV, Microsoft announced launch dates at its 2005 Electronic Entertainment Expo press conference. Launching in <a href="/north-america/3035-1664/" data-ref-id="3035-1664">North America</a> on November 22, 2005, December 2, 2005 in <a href="/europe/3035-289/" data-ref-id="3035-289">Europe</a>, and December 12, 2005 in <a href="/japan/3035-37/" data-ref-id="3035-37">Japan</a>, the Xbox 360 has gone on to sell more than 80 million units as of Oct. 17, 2013.</p><p>In a blog post by Xbox head <a href="/phil-spencer/3040-19275/" data-ref-id="3040-19275">Phil Spencer</a> on April 20th, 2016 it was announced that the Xbox 360 would cease manufacture though the online services provided via Xbox Live would remain ongoing for the forseeable future.</p><h2>Launch</h2><h3>North America - November 22, 2005</h3><ul><li><a href="/amped-3/3030-16647/" data-ref-id="3030-16647">Amped 3</a></li><li><a href="/call-of-duty-2/3030-2347/" data-ref-id="3030-2347">Call of Duty 2</a></li><li><a href="/condemned-criminal-origins/3030-8804/" data-ref-id="3030-8804">Condemned: Criminal Origins</a></li><li><a href="/fifa-06-road-to-fifa-world-cup/3030-27038/" data-ref-id="3030-27038">FIFA 06: Road to the FIFA World Cup</a></li><li><a href="/gun/3030-8873/" data-ref-id="3030-8873">GUN</a></li><li><a href="/kameo-elements-of-power/3030-19228/" data-ref-id="3030-19228">Kameo: Elements of Power</a></li><li><a href="/madden-nfl-06/3030-6648/" data-ref-id="3030-6648">Madden NFL 06</a></li><li><a href="/nba-2k6/3030-21363/" data-ref-id="3030-21363">NBA 2K6</a></li><li><a href="/nba-live-06/3030-7206/" data-ref-id="3030-7206">NBA Live 06</a></li><li><a href="/need-for-speed-most-wanted/3030-12976/" data-ref-id="3030-12976">Need for Speed: Most Wanted</a></li><li><a href="/nhl-2k6/3030-9031/" data-ref-id="3030-9031">NHL 2K6</a></li><li><a href="/perfect-dark-zero/3030-14558/" data-ref-id="3030-14558">Perfect Dark Zero</a></li><li><a href="/peter-jacksons-king-kong-the-official-game-of-the-movie/3030-9458/" data-ref-id="3030-9458">Peter Jackson's King Kong: The Official Game of the Movie</a></li><li><a href="/project-gotham-racing-3/3030-19809/" data-ref-id="3030-19809">Project Gotham Racing 3</a></li><li><a href="/quake-4/3030-13683/" data-ref-id="3030-13683">Quake 4</a></li><li><a href="/ridge-racer-6/3030-2324/" data-ref-id="3030-2324">Ridge Racer 6</a></li><li><a href="/tiger-woods-pga-tour-06/3030-3650/" data-ref-id="3030-3650">Tiger Woods PGA Tour 06</a></li><li><a href="/tony-hawks-american-wasteland/3030-7222/" data-ref-id="3030-7222">Tony Hawk's American Wasteland</a></li></ul><h3>Europe - An Xbox 360 with an updated look to closer resemble Microsoft's <a href="//www.giantbomb.com/xbox-one/3045-145/" data-ref-id="3045-145">Xbox One</a> console. The Xbox 360 E comes with the same internals as the "S" model, but has one fewer USB port, no S/PDIF connection, and a 3.5mm composite A/V connection.</p><h3>Xbox 360 E 250 GB S</figcaption></figure><p>The New Xbox 360 Announced at E3 2010 this smaller console features 802.11n wifi built in and a 250GB hard drive. It is also Kinect ready, meaning that the camera will be powered by the console and does not need a separate power supply like the older consoles do. Microsoft also claims that the system will run quieter than previous versions, dubbed "Whisper quiet". The new console will retail for $299.99 and began shipping to retailers June 14, 2010. All previous versions of the Xbox 360 have been reduced by 50 dollars. This model was updated in late 2012 to include the pack in game <a href="/forza-motorsport-4/3030-33400/" data-ref-id="3030-33400">Forza 4</a> and a download code for <a href="/the-elder-scrolls-v-skyrim/3030-33394/" data-ref-id="3030-33394">Elder scrolls V: Skyrim</a>. A</p><p>As an interesting note at the end of their E3 conference Microsoft also announced that all those in attendance would be getting a free new Xbox 360 S (later received in the mail).</p><h3> </h3><h3>Xbox 360 S 250 GB Kinect Bundle</h3><p>On November 16, 2010 Microsoft release a bundle of a standard 250 gigabyte Xbox 360 came with the motion camera system <a href="/kinect-support/3015-3249/" data-ref-id="3015-3249">Kinect</a> and a copy of <a href="/kinect-adventures/3030-31704/" data-ref-id="3030-31704">Kinect Adventures</a>. It retailed for $399.99.</p><p> </p><h3>Xbox 360 S 4 GB</h3><p>The 4 gigabyte Xbox 360 "s" features 802.11n wi-fi built in and has a matte finish rather than a the glossy finish of the 250 gigabyte model. It had a starting retail price of $199.99. In early 2012 all models where updated to be a matte finish.</p><h3> </h3><h3>Xbox 360 S 4 GB Kinect Bundle</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352686-xbox360_kinect.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-2352686" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.75213675213675" data-width="468" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 468px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:75.2%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352686-xbox360_kinect.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-2352686"><img alt="4GB Kinect Bundle" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352686-xbox360_kinect.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352686-xbox360_kinect.jpg 468w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352686-xbox360_kinect.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="4GB Kinect Bundle" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352686-xbox360_kinect.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352686-xbox360_kinect.jpg 468w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352686-xbox360_kinect.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a><figcaption>4GB Kinect Bundle</figcaption></figure><p>On November 16, 2010 Microsoft release a bundle of a standard 4 gigabyte Xbox 360 came with the motion camera system <a href="/kinect-support/3015-3249/" data-ref-id="3015-3249">Kinect</a> and a copy of <a href="/kinect-adventures/3030-31704/" data-ref-id="3030-31704">Kinect Adventures</a>. It retailed for $299.99. The system's specifications were virtually identical to the Xbox 360 Premium at the time. The system, wireless controller, and headset were painted in "Spartan green and gold," and the case sported the Halo 3 logo. The system came with an exclusive Dashboard theme and a Play and Charge Kit for the wireless controller.</p><h3>Resident Evil 5 Edition</h3><figure data-align="right" RE5 Editon</figcaption></figure><p>On February 4, 2009 before the launch of <a href="/resident-evil-5/3030-20569/" data-ref-id="3030-20569">Resident Evil 5</a>, Microsoft announced the Resident Evil Limited Edition of the Xbox 360. Edition</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/6/66077/1186669-mw2360.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1186669" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.77519379844961" Edition was a Limited Edition release of the Elite version of the console with a few upgraded features. With an MSRP of $399.99 USD the console was released in conjunction with Modern Warfare 2 on November 10th, 2009. This Limited Edition was packaged with a 250 GB hard drive, a copy of Modern Warfare 2, two black wireless controllers, a black headset, and a modified case design. Microsoft worked exclusively with Infinity Ward's art designers to produce a unique black and gray military styled case that matches Modern Warfare 2.</p><h3> </h3><h3>Xbox 360 Premium</h3><p>The Xbox 360 Premium was identical to the Xbox 360 Pro configuration but contained an older CPU architecture. Manufacturing for the Premium branded units ceased in August 2007.</p><p> </p><h3>Xbox 360 Core</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-2352653" data-size="small" data-ratio="1.5228426395939" data-width="591" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 591px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:152.3%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-2352653"><img alt="Xbox 360 Core" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 420px) 100vw, 420px" data-width="420" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg 591w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg 420w"><noscript><img alt="Xbox 360 Core" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg 591w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352653-xbox360_core1.jpg 420w" sizes="(max-width: 420px) 100vw, 420px" data-width="420"></noscript></a><figcaption>Xbox 360 Core</figcaption></figure><p>The Xbox 360 Core was the barebones 360 model that carried an MSRP of $279.99 and was similar to the current Arcade configuration. It included a wired controller, had no HDMI port, and did not include any kind of storage. The Xbox 360 Core was often seen as a misstep because its production meant that developers could not take advantage of the features Xbox 360 HDD in their games, since not all users would have one. It's main benefit to Microsoft was in marketing the platform when it was launched, as they were able to state that consumers could buy an Xbox 360 for "under $300," even though the more desirable Xbox 360 Premium was close to $400 USD at the time.</p><h3>Xbox 360 Pro</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-2352652" data-size="small" data-ratio="1.47375" data-width="800" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 800px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:147.4%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-2352652"><img alt="Xbox 360 Pro" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 434px) 100vw, 434px" data-width="434" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg 800w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg 434w"><noscript><img alt="Xbox 360 Pro" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg 800w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352652-xbox_3602.jpg 434w" sizes="(max-width: 434px) 100vw, 434px" data-width="434"></noscript></a><figcaption>Xbox 360 Pro</figcaption></figure><p>The Xbox 360 Pro, available in the "Go Pro" bundle, had an MSRP of $249.99 USD and replaced the Xbox 360 Premium SKU. Included in the bundle were all the features found in the Xbox 360 Arcade, as well as a 60 GB hard drive and a hybrid composite/component cable. The pre-loaded, detachable 60GB hard drive came with game demos, video clips and a free Live Arcade game: Hexic HD. The hard drive allowed for the storage of downloaded content, backwards compatibility with original Xbox games, and storage of game saves. The Xbox 360 Pro bundle carried an MSRP of $299.99 USD. Prior to August 2008, the included HDD was only 20GB. For the 2007 holiday shopping season, Microsoft bundled copies of <a href="/forza-motorsport-2/3030-5881/" data-ref-id="3030-5881">Forza Motorsport 2</a> and <a href="/marvel-ultimate-alliance/3030-7527/" data-ref-id="3030-7527">Marvel: Ultimate Alliance</a> with the Xbox 360 Pro. In 2008, the holiday bundle included <a href="/lego-indiana-jones-the-original-adventures/3030-20534/" data-ref-id="3030-20534">Lego Indiana Jones</a> and <a href="/kung-fu-panda/3030-20640/" data-ref-id="3030-20640">Kung Fu Panda</a>. In 2009, reduced the price of the Xbox 360 Elite to $299.99, and phased out the Xbox 360 Pro.</p><h3>Xbox 360 Arcade</h3><p>An entry level Xbox 360 that replaced the now discontinued Xbox 360 Core. The Xbox 360 Arcade sports a wireless controller, 256 MB memory unit (Which has now been replaced with an internal 256mb chip in the 'Jasper' version of consoles), composite AV cable, HDMI 1.2 output, and 5 Xbox Live Arcade titles: <a href="/boom-boom-rocket/3030-1826/" data-ref-id="3030-1826">Boom Boom Rocket</a>, <a href="/feeding-frenzy/3030-18440/" data-ref-id="3030-18440">Feeding Frenzy</a>, <a href="/luxor-2/3030-12020/" data-ref-id="3030-12020">Luxor 2</a>, <a href="/pac-man-championship-edition/3030-19552/" data-ref-id="3030-19552">Pac-Man Championship Edition</a>, and <a href="/uno/3030-12083/" data-ref-id="3030-12083">Uno</a> on a single disk. This disc also includes a "Welcome Video" and several game trailers/demos. Officially announce on October 22, 2007, the Xbox 360 Arcade has a MSRP of $199.99 USD. Recently Microsoft confirmed that they are now putting internal memory into the Xbox 360 Arcade. This storage will be the same size as the previous external memory units: 256MB. Xbox 360 Arcade systems packaged for the 2008 holiday shopping season are bundled with a copy of <a href="/sega-superstars-tennis/3030-20578/" data-ref-id="3030-20578">Sega Superstars Tennis</a>.</p><h3>Xbox 360 Elite</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-2352654" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.72" data-width="900" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 900px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:72.0%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-2352654"><img alt="Xbox 360 Elite" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg 900w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="Xbox 360 Elite" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg 900w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/2/26636/2352654-xbox360_elite_04.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a><figcaption>Xbox 360 Elite</figcaption></figure><p>The Elite is currently the mid-end Xbox 360 configuration carrying an MSRP of $249.99 USD. It has all of the features of the Xbox 360 Pro, but comes with an upgraded 120 GB hard drive and has a matte black finish with matching controller and headset. For the 2008 holiday shopping season, The Elite model came packed with<a href="/lego-indiana-jones-the-original-adventures/3030-20534/" data-ref-id="3030-20534"> Lego Indiana Jones</a> and <a href="/kung-fu-panda/3030-20640/" data-ref-id="3030-20640">Kung Fu Panda</a>. In 2009 there was a bundle which included both <a href="/fable-ii/3030-20514/" data-ref-id="3030-20514">Fable 2</a> and <a href="/halo-3/3030-9993/" data-ref-id="3030-9993">Halo 3</a>. This was followed with a bundle containing <a href="/lego-batman-the-video-game/3030-20822/" data-ref-id="3030-20822">Lego Batman</a> and <a href="/pure/3030-20957/" data-ref-id="3030-20957">Pure</a>. In 2009, Microsoft dropped the price of the Xbox 360 Elite to $299.99, most likely to match the price of Sony's new PS3 slim carrying the same price. In 2010, Microsoft introduced a redesigned Xbox 360 and reduced the price of the 360 Elite to $249.99.</p><h3>Xbox 360 Splinter Cell Conviction Bundle</h3><p>Released with little to no fanfare, the <a href="/tom-clancys-splinter-cell-conviction/3030-20464/" data-ref-id="3030-20464">Splinter Cell Conviction</a> bundle is quite similar to its immediate predecessor, the <a href="/final-fantasy-xiii/3030-20664/" data-ref-id="3030-20664">Final Fantasy XIII</a> bundle. It includes a black Xbox 360 Console, a 250GB HDD, two black Xbox 360 controllers, and a copy of <a href="/tom-clancy/3025-556/" data-ref-id="3025-556">Tom Clancy</a>'s Splinter Cell Conviction. Unlike many of the special edition Xbox 360 bundles, this one does not feature any unique artwork or designs on any of the included hardware. It retailed for $399.99 US.</p><h2>Games</h2><p>The Xbox 360 has a large array of games starting in November 2005. On launch, Microsoft's first party titles included <a href="/perfect-dark-zero/3030-14558/" data-ref-id="3030-14558">Perfect Dark Zero</a>, <a href="/kameo-elements-of-power/3030-19228/" data-ref-id="3030-19228">Kameo: Elements of Power</a>, and <a href="/project-gotham-racing-3/3030-19809/" data-ref-id="3030-19809">PGR 3</a>. Activision's <a href="/call-of-duty-2/3030-2347/" data-ref-id="3030-2347">Call of Duty 2</a> introduces console gamers to the series and became the biggest game on Xbox Live during launch. Later in 2006, Epic Games released <a href="/gears-of-war-2/3030-20662/" data-ref-id="3030-20662">Gears of War</a>, what was considered to be the "killer app" of the Xbox 360. Thanks to the game's impressive graphics and multiplayer, the game became a big hit. 2007 would follow many games like <a href="/halo-3/3030-9993/" data-ref-id="3030-9993">Halo 3</a> (one of the most hyped games of the year), <a href="/mass-effect/3030-16909/" data-ref-id="3030-16909">Mass Effect</a>, and <a href="/call-of-duty-4-modern-warfare/3030-2133/" data-ref-id="3030-2133">Call of Duty 4: Modern Warfare</a>, which broke many records on Xbox Live when it was released, with its <a href="/modern-warfare-2/3030-24713/" data-ref-id="3030-24713">sequel</a> surpassing it. Many other sequels would be released including <a href="/fable-ii/3030-20514/" data-ref-id="3030-20514">Fable 2</a> and <a href="/banjo-kazooie-nuts-bolts/3030-20586/" data-ref-id="3030-20586">Banjo Kazooie: Nuts and Bolts</a> within the later years.</p><p>One key feature to Xbox Live's success is the Xbox Live Arcade games. On launch, the 360 Premium bundle came packaged with<a href="/hexic/3030-18287/" data-ref-id="3030-18287"> Hexic HD</a>, a puzzle game created by <a href="/tetris/3025-291/" data-ref-id="3025-291">Tetris</a> creator <a href="/alexey-pajitnov/3040-9332/" data-ref-id="3040-9332">Alexey Pajitnov</a>. Other launch titles include<a href="/geometry-wars-retro-evolved/3030-11099/" data-ref-id="3030-11099"> Geometry Wars: Retro Evolved</a> and<a href="/marble-blast-ultra/3030-8047/" data-ref-id="3030-8047"> Marble Blast Ultra</a>. In the beginning, Microsoft restricted Arcade game sizes to no more than 50 MB big due to the Core model and its memory card. Later, when the 256 MB memory card was released, the game size limit was expanded. Today you're able to get full games online and games can be installed to your hard drive.</p><h3>Compatibility with original Xbox Games</h3><p>By and large the Xbox 360 is not compatible with original Xbox games out of the box. Instead Microsoft provided software emulation for selected titles. The emulation is based on games with similar architecture to each other. This means that from a distance the list of compatible titles may look strange with such inclusions as <a href="//www.giantbomb.com/barbie-horse-adventure-wild-horse-rescue/3030-7844/" data-ref-id="3030-7844">Barbie's Horse Adventure</a> while many best selling or critically acclaimed titles are seemingly ignored.</p><p>The emulation is not perfect and in a lot of case games feature glitches that were not present in the original version. Glitches can go from minor (slowdown, framerate issues) to sever (some glitches cause games to full on crash) Thirteen games were pulled from the service presumable due to such issue. (Seven of which were later reinstated)</p><p>Microsoft stopped updating the Xbox emulator in 2007. According to Wikipedia the final total of backwards compatible titles is 476 title making up approximately half of all Xbox games..</p><p> </p><h2>New Xbox Experience (NXE)</h2><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-365903" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.61888111888112" data-width="572" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 572px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:61.9%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-365903"><img alt="The old Xbox 360 Dashboard" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg 572w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="The old Xbox 360 Dashboard" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg 572w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1694/365903-360_dashboard.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a><figcaption>The old Xbox 360 Dashboard</figcaption></figure><p>Since launch the main way of interacting with the Xbox 360 has been using the 'Dashboard', a menu system split into sections by 'Blades'; initially the 'Dashboard' consisted of four 'Blades:' Live, Games, Media and Settings; a blade was later added which separated the Xbox Live Marketplace from the Xbox Live 'Blade'. At the 2008 Electronic Entertainment Expo (E3) Microsoft announced it would be completely redesigning the Xbox Dashboard into a more conventional menu system dubbed the <a href="/new-xbox-experience/3015-2426/" data-ref-id="3015-2426">New Xbox Experience</a>.</p><p>The New Xbox Experience (NXE) is designed to be more user friendly and to be expandable as new content is added, it takes several design cues from the likes of Apple and Nintendo, and introduces several new features such as Avatars and Live Party. The New Xbox Experience was released on November 19, 2008.</p><h3>Notable features of the NXE:</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/9734/769073-3.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-769073" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.56111111111111" data-width="540" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 540px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:56.1%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/9734/769073-3.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-769073"><img alt="The New Xbox Experience" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/9734/769073-3.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/9734/769073-3.jpg 540w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/0/9734/769073-3.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/9734/769073-3.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="The New Xbox Experience" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/9734/769073-3.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/9734/769073-3.jpg 540w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/0/9734/769073-3.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/9734/769073-3.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a><figcaption>The New Xbox Experience</figcaption></figure><ul><li>Avatars: A 3D representation of the user, replaces the current Gamercard; however Microsoft assure gamers they can still use their old Gamercard.</li><li>Live Party: A group of up to 8 people, allows users to voice chat independent of which game they are each playing.</li><li>Play From Drive: Allows players to copy disc content over to the HDD in order to cut down load times and DVD drive noise. The disc of the game played from the HDD is still required to be in the DVD drive.</li><li>Deleting Zero-Point games: The ability to delete games with no achievements unlocked has become possible, so that players may improve their ratio of possible achievements to ones gained.</li><li>Netflix: The Xbox 360 gained the ability to stream movies from Netfilx to view on your TV. This feature is only available to gold members and requires a Netflix paid account.</li></ul><p>The new Xbox 360 Guide (accessible through the Xbox button on the controller) will mimic the interface of the "Blade" dashboard system. It's accessible in all Xbox 360 games to manage messages/invites, create parties, view player statistics, et cetera.</p><p>The NXE update was distributed in the fall of 2008, and took 128 Mb of space to install. Those not meeting this requirement (The Arcade and Core SKUs not having hard drives) were given a free memory unit (512MB) by Microsoft or the option to buy a 20GB Hard Drive at $20.</p><h3>Features after NXE:</h3><p>At CES 2009 Microsoft's Robby Bach announced <a href="/xbox-live-primetime/3015-2647/" data-ref-id="3015-2647">Xbox Live Primetime</a>. Primetime was the first channel on Xbox Live to use scheduled programming at specific time so you can find friends &amp; experience live events. One of the first games to run in Primetime was <a href="/1-vs-100/3030-25031/" data-ref-id="3030-25031">1 VS 100</a>, which has since been discontinued. On November 17, 2009, Microsoft released another new update for the Xbox 360. With this new update, Microsoft made available custom hubs for <a href="/facebook-connectivity/3015-3476/" data-ref-id="3015-3476">Facebook</a> and <a href="/twitter-support/3015-3827/" data-ref-id="3015-3827">Twitter</a>, along with added features like posting pictures of your games on your <a href="/facebook-connectivity/3015-3476/" data-ref-id="3015-3476">Facebook</a> page. Other features include Last.fm, Zune HD, and accessing news stations like MSNBC.</p><h2>Criticisms</h2><p>There are a number of criticism that are often leveraged against the Xbox 360, the main one being unreliable hardware quality; however, excessive DVD drive noise and a confusing amount of hardware configurations are also targeted by critics of the system.</p><h3>'The Red Ring of Death'</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1694/326567-red_ring_of_death_1_.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-326567" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.86666666666667" data-width="450" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 450px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:86.7%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1694/326567-red_ring_of_death_1_.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-326567"><img alt="Red Ring of Death" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1694/326567-red_ring_of_death_1_.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1694/326567-red_ring_of_death_1_.jpg 450w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1694/326567-red_ring_of_death_1_.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="Red Ring of Death" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1694/326567-red_ring_of_death_1_.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1694/326567-red_ring_of_death_1_.jpg 450w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1694/326567-red_ring_of_death_1_.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a><figcaption>Red Ring of Death</figcaption></figure><p>The Xbox 360 has gained a reputation for a high failure rate, sometimes rumored to be as high as 30% although Microsoft have denied the failure rate is that high; they have not released an official failure rate. The most common hardware failure is the General Hardware Failure, denoted by the bottom two and upper right quadrant of the Ring of Light flashing red; leading to the failure being dubbed the ' <a href="/red-ring-of-death/3015-290/" data-ref-id="3015-290">Red Ring of Death</a>'. This failure renders the console unable to boot or 'bricked' and the only official course of action for the consumer being to call Xbox support to ship the console back to Microsoft where it is either repaired or replaced. While there is no official course of action on fixing the Red Ring of Death there are some unofficial solutions to try. The most popular is called the "towel trick" in which you take everything off of your Xbox 360, your hard-drive, A/V cables, etc. The only thing you want plugged in is the power supply. Now you wrap it in three (3) large towels (the ones you would use to dry yourself off after a shower) and turn it on. Let it sit running for 20-30 minutes, turn it off, and let it cool off for another 15. Then turn it on and it should work. *Note this is not a permanent solution.*</p><p>No official reason has been given by Microsoft as to why this error is so common place, however most speculation points towards insufficient cooling around the GPU leading to a warping of the motherboard. Microsoft has taken steps to solve this problem by adding an additional heat sink to the GPU in later units and units returned from repair. These changes were included in a chipset refresh codenamed 'Falcon' which also includes a 65nm CPU to further reduce heat. An as yet unreleased chip set refresh, codenamed 'Jasper,' will introduce a 65nm GPU and is hoped to solve the 'Red Ring of Death' problem.</p><p>As well as these hardware revisions Microsoft has increased the Xbox 360 warranty to 3 years, however this is only to cover the 'Red Ring of Death' all other hardware problems are only covered for 1 year; this was reported to have cost Microsoft $1 billion.</p><p><i>Note</i>: the new "XBOX 360 'S'" does not feature the red LEDs behind the power button. Microsoft removed this particular error message because of the bad connotations associated with this.</p><h3>DVD Drive Problems</h3><p>The DVD Drive is often the target of criticism, mostly for the excessive noise produced and an apparent tendency for scratching discs. These issues are less apparent in later models of the 360 as Microsoft have replaced the initial DVD drive with a quieter model from BenQ.</p><h3>Power Adapter Size</h3><p>The Xbox 360's power adapter is significantly larger than similar adapters on previous consoles. This criticism was mostly vocal at the beginning of the Xbox 360's retail life, as Microsoft has reduced the power adapter's size over the life of the console.</p><h3>Xbox Live Arcade File Size Restriction</h3><p>Initially Xbox Live Arcade games had to come in under the 50 MB file size restriction. While many people felt that that 50MB was too small to create games this limitation allowed 360 owners without the hard drive to enjoy all of the content of XBLA at that time. Over time Microsoft has relaxed restrictions to coincide with the release of larger memory units. Currently the size limit is 2GB and this is a limitation of the backend of service itself rather than an arbitrary limit imposed by Microsoft.</p>

<Platform 'Nintendo Entertainment System'>
Nintendo Entertainment System
1983-07-15 00:00:00
Nintendo

61910000
<h2>Overview</h2><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816794-nes_logo.png" data-ref-id="1300-816794" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.40042826552463" data-width="467" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 467px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:40.0%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816794-nes_logo.png" data-ref-id="1300-816794"><img alt="The Nintendo Entertainment System logo" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/816794-nes_logo.png" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816794-nes_logo.png 467w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/816794-nes_logo.png 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></a><figcaption>The Nintendo Entertainment System logo</figcaption></figure><p>The Nintendo Entertainment System (often abbreviated as "NES," colloquially referred to as simply "Nintendo," and dubbed as the "Control Deck" on boxes and in documentation), also known as the Famicom, was <a href="/nintendo/3010-90/" data-ref-id="3010-90">Nintendo</a>'s second attempt to attract home consumers, following the modest success of the <a href="/color-tvgame-15/3055-6115/" data-ref-id="3055-6115">Color TV Game</a> in Japan.</p><p>In <a href="/japan/3035-37/" data-ref-id="3035-37">Japan </a>and many other <a href="/asia/3035-1663/" data-ref-id="3035-1663">Asian </a>countries, the NES was known as the Family Computer (or as it came to be later known, the Famicom); in some Asian countries, it was known as the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tata_Group" rel="nofollow" data-ref-id="false">Tata</a> Famicom. It released in Japan in July 15, 1983, on the same day as <a href="/sega/3010-62/" data-ref-id="3010-62">Sega</a>'s <a href="/sega-sg-1000/3045-141/" data-ref-id="3045-141">SG-1000</a>, which it beat with its technical superiority and stronger software library. The Famicom <a href="http://www.usgamer.net/articles/why-did-atari-fail-in-japan" rel="nofollow" data-ref-id="false">offered</a> unrivalled technical power in its time for the lowest possible price, selling over 1.4 million units in its first year and establishing console gaming as a mainstream market in Japan, a country that was previously dominated by <a href="/arcade/3045-84/" data-ref-id="3045-84">arcades</a> and home computers (such as the <a href="/nec-pc-8801/3045-109/" data-ref-id="3045-109">PC-88</a>, <a href="/nec-pc-9801/3045-112/" data-ref-id="3045-112">PC-98</a>, <a href="/fm-7/3045-114/" data-ref-id="3045-114">FM-7</a>, <a href="/sharp-x1/3045-113/" data-ref-id="3045-113">X1</a>, and <a href="/msx/3045-15/" data-ref-id="3045-15">MSX</a>).</p><p>The 8-bit video game console was released by Nintendo as the NES in <a href="/north-america/3035-1664/" data-ref-id="3035-1664">North America</a>, <a href="/europe/3035-289/" data-ref-id="3035-289">Europe</a> and <a href="/australia/3035-292/" data-ref-id="3035-292">Australia </a>in 1985. After the North American video game market crash of 1983, the NES was the perfect revitalization. It went on to become the best-selling video game console of all time (up until the <a href="/playstation/3045-22/" data-ref-id="3045-22">PlayStation</a>). Some of the <a href="/hollywood/3035-642/" data-ref-id="3035-642">Hollywood</a> stars at the time who <a href="http://archive.org/stream/raze-magazine-05/Raze_05_Mar_1991#page/n17/mode/2up/search/billion" rel="nofollow" data-ref-id="false">owned</a> the NES at the time included <a href="/michael-j-fox/3040-97946/" data-ref-id="3040-97946">Michael J. Fox</a>, <a href="/robin-williams/3040-55806/" data-ref-id="3040-55806">Robin Williams</a>, Whoopi Goldberg, Tom Hanks, <a href="/bruce-willis/3040-89593/" data-ref-id="3040-89593">Bruce Willis</a>, and Tom Cruise.</p><p>The NES introduced many conventions that have become standard, including game controller layout, D-pad, third-party software licensing, and the business strategy of selling hardware at a loss and profiting from licensed software.</p><h2>History</h2><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/9/91778/1702011-nes_control_deck_boxed.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1702011" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.71255060728745" data-width="494" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 494px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:71.3%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/9/91778/1702011-nes_control_deck_boxed.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1702011"><img alt="A boxed NES Control Deck." src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/9/91778/1702011-nes_control_deck_boxed.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/9/91778/1702011-nes_control_deck_boxed.jpg 494w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/9/91778/1702011-nes_control_deck_boxed.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/9/91778/1702011-nes_control_deck_boxed.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></a><figcaption>A boxed NES Control Deck.</figcaption></figure><p>The year was 1981 and after the success of <a href="/donkey-kong/3030-311/" data-ref-id="3030-311">Donkey Kong</a> and its successful release on the <a href="/colecovision/3045-47/" data-ref-id="3045-47">ColecoVision</a> where it quickly became the killer app for the console Nintendo turned to then head of its video game division <a href="/masayuki-uemura/3040-69066/" data-ref-id="3040-69066">Masayuki Uemura</a> to design a cartridge-based home console. While most of the companies engineers continued to work on the <a href="/game-watch/3025-1183/" data-ref-id="3025-1183">Game &amp; Watch</a> product line, Uemura set to work researching and designing what would later become the Nintendo Entertainment System. As more and more engineers began to transition over to help Uemura design the machine several key discussions arose to determine the internal workings of the machine.</p><h4>Selecting the CPU:</h4><p>The most significant decision made being the choice of CPU used in the console. Uemura wanted the CPU to be small enough to allow a sound chip to be integrated onto the board to reduce costs and due to Nintendo's relationship with chip manufacturer Ricoh whose 6502 processor met the requirements the initial reaction was to use the Ricoh 6502 processor. Within the company however several of the engineers disputed this choice in favour of the Z80 processor to allow the source code of the game Donkey Kong to be used. As the chief engineer though Uemura selected to use the Ricoh 6502 processor and so the company was forced to develop Donkey Kong from scratch. Another key decision would be the selection of the color palette of the console and so Uemura went to <a href="/shigeru-miyamoto/3040-614/" data-ref-id="3040-614">Shigeru Miyamoto</a> to assist with the color choice by asking him what and how many colors would be needed to recreate his games.</p><h4>The design of the controller:</h4><p>Another heated aspect of the design within the company was that of the controller. Having designed arcade games in the past, several of the engineers believed a joystick controller (similar to that of the <a href="/atari-2600/3045-40/" data-ref-id="3045-40">Atari 2600</a>) should be the included with the console. One engineer who worked on the project however having just assisted the Game &amp; Watch team with the creation of the Donkey Kong Game &amp; Watch took the control unit created for it, removed the screen and connected it to a Famicom system as a test. Realising that the Famicom controllers should utilise the revolutionary D-pad created for the Donkey Kong Game &amp; Watch and that the D-pad was intuitive enough to use that players could focus on the screen opposed to the controller so it was decided that the controller design should incorporate a D-pad over a joystick.</p><h4>The decision to use cartridges for games:</h4><p>The choice to use cartridges came from the decision that the sole purpose of the console would be to play video games meaning that the data on the cartridge wouldn't need to be altered after release. Thus the company decided to use ROM data and styled the Japanese cartridges after audio cassettes to allow Japanese consumers to use pre-existing household furniture and containers to store their game collection.</p><h4>The origins of Famicom red:</h4><p>The iconic Famicom red color choice came when the discussion of what color to make the console arose and due to Nintendo president <a href="/hiroshi-yamauchi/3040-615/" data-ref-id="3040-615">Hiroshi Yamauchi's </a>favourite color being red the decision was made to use the same shade of red as the president's scarf.</p><h4>The origins of the name Famicom:</h4><p>The Japanese name of 'Family Computer' (later Famicom) was not given to the console until shortly before its release and came from a conversation between Uemura and his wife. Uemura, who often discussed his work with his wife, explained one evening that the console was still without a name and despite personal computers already existing in Japan that the console shouldn't be seen as a "personal" device and instead one for the entire family. Thus Uemura explained it should be called the "Family Computer" to which his wife responded "Okay but it has to be Famicom. You have to make it shorter.". Liking the name "Famicom" Uemura took the idea straight to company president Yaumauchi the next day and explained the reasoning behind the name but Yaumauchi was not in favour of the name claiming "No, it's not a good idea to shorten the words at the beginning. If people want to start calling it that later, that's okay, but at the start we need to call it 'Family Computer'.".</p><h4>The initial Japanese release:</h4><p>The console was first released in Japan on July 15, 1983 with the three launch titles of <a href="/donkey-kong/3030-311/" data-ref-id="3030-311">Donkey Kong</a>, <a href="/donkey-kong-jr/3030-19416/" data-ref-id="3030-19416">Donkey Kong Jr.</a>, and <a href="/popeye/3030-14419/" data-ref-id="3030-14419">Popeye</a> available. The console sold around 400,000 units in its first year though approximately 100,000 units were returned as faulty due to the initial wave of consoles being prone to crashes due to defects in some of the graphics chips created by Ricoh as well as the issue of owners damaging the controllers of the console which were hard-wired into the console to save on costs over implementing a joypad connector to the console. This decision was later reverted to allow for damaged controllers to be easily replaced via simply buying and plugging in a replacement controller.</p><p>By the end of 1983 the initial wave of the Famicom stock had sold out but when retailers in February of the following year kept on requesting additional stock the console was resupplied complete with a new motherboard to fix the issue with the graphics chips and the Famicom swiftly became incredibly popular.</p><h4>Entering the American market:</h4><p>In an effort to enter the North American market, Nintendo negotiated with Atari to release the Famicom as the Nintendo Advanced Video Gaming System but the deal would fail to materialise. In June of 1985, Nintendo unveiled the North American version of the Famicom (the Nintendo Entertainment System) which had undergone several cosmetic changes from the original Famicom system. For instance, the console was stylised to make it look more like a VCR and was colored with shades of grey to make it blend in better with the traditional television setup. Its controllers were also redesigned to accommodate for the larger hands of American children, the controllers were made detachable from the console based off the past experience with the non-detachable controllers of the Famicom and the problems which arose due to this design aspect. The built-in microphone of the controller was removed to save costs and because of the belief that the intent to use the microphone for karaoke would not be as appealing as it was in Japan.</p><p>On October 18, 1985, the NES was released, along with eighteen launch titles. Two boxed sets were released, the Deluxe Set (console, <a href="/rob/3005-1707/" data-ref-id="3005-1707">R.O.B</a>., <a href="/light-gun/3015-2354/" data-ref-id="3015-2354">Zapper</a>, two controllers, <a href="/duck-hunt/3030-2758/" data-ref-id="3030-2758">Duck Hunt</a>, and <a href="/gyromite/3030-20055/" data-ref-id="3030-20055">Gyromite</a>) and the Control Deck (console, two controllers and <a href="/super-mario-bros/3030-15544/" data-ref-id="3030-15544">Super Mario Bros.</a>).</p><p>Nintendo initially had a hard time selling the NES to retailers due to most believing the video game home console market to have died with the crash of 1983. Realising this Nintendo marketed the NES as a toy opposed to a video game system. They packed in a light gun and a robot with the console and people started to pay attention. In December of 1985 Nintendo went to toy stores around New York City to try and sell the NES negotiating that if the consoles don't sell they will buy them back. This gave Nintendo a foothold but they still required getting the NES into the hands of more people if the product was to be a success.</p><p>The company then contacted Worlds of Wonder, a toy company who made two of the most popular toys of 1985, Lazer Tag and Teddy Ruxpin, claiming if they could get Nintendo into the same big department stores as their toys were in that they could have a percentage of Nintendo's sales. Worlds of Wonder agreed to this deal, so whenever a store called and wanted to order a toy, they would require that store to order 500 NES consoles. With this deal in place Nintendo had now made their first steps into the American market.</p><p>The NES was an enormous success in Japan and North America, dominating the competition in both regions. In comparison to its considerable success in Japan and North America, however, the NES had much less success in Europe and <a href="/south-america/3035-2906/" data-ref-id="3035-2906">South America</a>, with <a title="Sega" href="/sega/3010-62/" data-ref-id="3010-62">Sega</a>'s <a title="Sega Master System" href="/sega-master-system/3045-8/" data-ref-id="3045-8">Master System</a> being significantly more successful than the NES in these regions. (<a href="http://www.nintendolife.com/news/2014/07/hardware_classics_sega_master_system" rel="nofollow" data-ref-id="false">Ref</a>) ("Retroinspection: Master System", <i>Retro Gamer, </i>issue 44, pages 4853)</p><h3>US Cumulative Sales</h3><ul><li>1985: <strong>90,000</strong> (<a href="/new-york-city/3035-109/" data-ref-id="3035-109">New York City</a>) (<a href="http://elafountain.escalonimaginario.com/comeback.html" rel="nofollow" data-ref-id="false">ref</a>) (<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/1986/09/27/business/video-games-once-zapped-in-comeback.html" rel="nofollow" data-ref-id="false">ref</a>)</li><li>1986: <strong>1,190,000</strong> (<a <strong>4,190,000</strong> (<a href="http://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1314&amp;dat=19880409&amp;id=klpWAAAAIBAJ&amp;sjid=mu8DAAAAIBAJ&amp;pg=4634,5262094" rel="nofollow" share</a>)</li><li>1991: <strong>30,000,000</strong> (<a href="http://books.google.co.uk/books?id=puMDAAAAMBAJ&amp;pg=PA75" rel="nofollow" data-ref-id="false">ref</a>)</li></ul><h2>Licensing</h2><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816796-nintendo_seal_of_quality.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-816796" data-size="small" data-ratio="1" data-width="150" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 150px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:100.0%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816796-nintendo_seal_of_quality.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-816796"><img alt="Nintendo's seal of quality" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px" data-width="150" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816796-nintendo_seal_of_quality.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816796-nintendo_seal_of_quality.jpg 150w"><noscript><img alt="Nintendo's seal of quality" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816796-nintendo_seal_of_quality.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/816796-nintendo_seal_of_quality.jpg 150w" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px" data-width="150"></noscript></a><figcaption>Nintendo's seal of quality</figcaption></figure><p>Nintendo's licensing techniques were both revolutionary and for a time, illegal. Nintendo had a veritable monopoly on the market at the time, so they encouraged developers to make games for their console. But, developers had to sign a contract stating they would only develop games for the NES. Also, a chip was instituted into the NES called the 10NES. If this same chip was not found in the cartridge, the game wouldn't load. Eventually, however, these business practices were ultimately outlawed.</p><p>Despite Nintendo's efforts, unlicensed games were still created for the system. Designers found ways to bypass the 10NES chip. One such way was to short circuit the chip, temporarily ceasing its function. However, <a href="/atari-games-corporation/3010-794/" data-ref-id="3010-794">Atari Games</a> created unlicensed software for the NES under the name <a href="/tengen/3010-752/" data-ref-id="3010-752">Tengen</a>. Tengen didn't want to be held liable for short-circuiting and possibly damaging the NES, so they devised a chip (nicknamed Rabbit) that disabled the 10NES chip. It was later discovered that their patent was acquired illegally, and thus, they were sued by Nintendo and lost.</p><h2>Launch Games</h2><h3>Japan - July 15, 1983</h3><ul><li><a data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1705460" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.43833333333333" data-width="600" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 600px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:43.8%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1705460"><img alt="No Caption Provided" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg 600w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="No Caption Provided" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg 600w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg 480w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/12/121177/1705460-816804_10nes_super.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a></figure><ul><li><b>CPU</b>: 8-bit microprocessor (by Ricoh, based on MOS Technology 6502 core) operating at 1.79MHz on NTSC systems and 1.66MHz on PAL systems.</li><li><b>Memory</b>: 2 kB main RAM (random-access memory), 2 kB video RAM, 49,128 bytes ROM (read-only memory)</li><li><b>Video</b>: Custom-made picture processing unit (by Ricoh) named RP2C02 (in NTSC models, operates at 5.37 MHz) and RP2C07 (in PAL models, operates at 5.32 MHz)</li><li>Color palette of 53 colors (48 colors and 5 grays), 25 colors on one scanline</li><li>64 sprites displayed on the screen simultaneously (sprites can be either 8 x 8 pixels or 8 x 16 pixels)</li><li>Display resolution is 256 x 240 pixels (effective resolution of 256 x 224 pixels)</li><li><b>Audio</b>: Ricoh RP2A03 on NTSC systems and Ricoh RP2A07 on PAL systems. Has 5 separate audio channels. Two pulse-wave, one triangle-wave, one white-noise and one DPCM channel.</li></ul><h3>NES-001 vs. NES-101</h3><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843358-tumblr_l7qqlfeflj1qa6wvao1_400.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1843358" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.71538461538462" data-width="390" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 390px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:71.5%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843358-tumblr_l7qqlfeflj1qa6wvao1_400.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1843358"><img alt="The box of NES-101" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843358-tumblr_l7qqlfeflj1qa6wvao1_400.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843358-tumblr_l7qqlfeflj1qa6wvao1_400.jpg 390w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843358-tumblr_l7qqlfeflj1qa6wvao1_400.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="The box of NES-101" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843358-tumblr_l7qqlfeflj1qa6wvao1_400.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843358-tumblr_l7qqlfeflj1qa6wvao1_400.jpg 390w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843358-tumblr_l7qqlfeflj1qa6wvao1_400.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a><figcaption>The box of NES-101</figcaption></figure><p>After the success of the NES, Nintendo introduced the NES-101, a new budget priced 'entry level' model of the console on October 15, 1993. Known as the top-loader, this version is nearly identical to the original model, but it has several key differences. The main difference, and the reason for its nickname, is the fact that cartridges are loaded into a slot on the top of the console, rather than through a tray at the front. It also sported a different color scheme and more round edged controllers similar in design to those of the <a href="/super-nintendo-entertainment-system/3045-9/" data-ref-id="3045-9">Super Nintendo Entertainment System</a>. It also featured a redesigned logo and modified circuit boards to improve the video output.NES-101 was known as HVC-101 in Japan, and was released on December 1, 1993.</p><h2>Accessories</h2><table><tbody><tr><th>Nintendo Zapper</th></tr><tr><td>The Zapper was a light gun that came bundled with the NES later on in its life span. The gun originally was gray, however to make it appear less threatening the zapper was later changed to orange. http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_medium/0/1992/1426307-acc_pad.jpg 480w"><noscript><img alt="No Caption Provided" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1992/1426307-acc_pad.jpg" 480px" data-width="480"></noscript></a></figure></td></tr></tbody></table><table><tbody><tr><th>NES Max</th></tr><tr><td>The NES Max was a popular controller because its built in turbo function was a new feature at the time.</td><td><figure data-align="left" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1992/1426306-acc_max.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1426306" data-size="small" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/1992/1426306-acc_max.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/1992/1426306-acc_max.jpg 380w, data-width="320"></noscript></a></figure></td></tr></tbody></table><table><tbody><tr><th>NES Four Score</th></tr><tr><td>The NES Four Score was a wired splitter that made it possible fore four players to simultaneously play on the NES. It offered options for turbo (for all connected players), and the ability to switch between two player and four player.</td><td><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843395-nes_four_score.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1843395" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.80597014925373" data-width="402" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 402px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:80.6%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843395-nes_four_score.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1843395"><img alt="No Caption Provided" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843395-nes_four_score.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843395-nes_four_score.jpg 402w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843395-nes_four_score.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="No Caption Provided" src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843395-nes_four_score.jpg" srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843395-nes_four_score.jpg 402w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843395-nes_four_score.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320"></noscript></a></figure></td></tr></tbody></table><table><tbody><tr><th>R.O.B.</th></tr><tr><td>R.O.B., an acronym for Robotic Operating Buddy, was the console's most infamous accessory. He was supposed to move colored discs to aid the player in compatible games, but he was so slow that it made gameplay almost impossible. Only two compatible games were ever released: <a href="/gyromite/3030-20055/" data-ref-id="3030-20055">Gyromite</a> and <a href="/stack-up/3030-19746/" data-ref-id="3030-19746">Stack-Up</a>.</td><td><figure data-align="right" data-img-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843490-r.o.b.stack_up.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1843490" data-size="small" data-ratio="0.81111111111111" data-width="450" data-embed-type="image" style="width: 450px"><a class="fluid-height" style="padding-bottom:81.1%" href="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843490-r.o.b.stack_up.jpg" data-ref-id="1300-1843490"><img alt="No Caption Provided" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" sizes="(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px" data-width="320" class="js-lazy-load-image" data-src="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843490-r.o.b.stack_up.jpg" data-srcset="http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/original/0/7465/1843490-r.o.b.stack_up.jpg 450w, http://static.giantbomb.com/uploads/scale_small/0/7465/1843490-r.o.b.stack_up.jpg 320w"><noscript><img alt="No Caption Provided"
